The Tusi of Xikang will sincerely welcome the entry of a total of 150,000 Tibetan troops who share the same religion with them. He said: "The Tibetan government is currently ruled by the 15-year-old Dalai Lama, but in fact it is ruled by the Dalai Lama's teacher, but he is now 70 years old and it is difficult to manage major affairs, so the real power is in the hands of the four major families. Because of their education and personal interests, they tend to be more pro-British than pro-Chinese. The Chinese government only has a branch of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission in Tibet, which is responsible for everything from education to diplomacy. There is no branch of the Central Bank in Tibet, and all remittances and transactions are handled by Indian banks. The Tibetan currency system is linked to the British pound sterling group, so the economic situation is more stable than in other parts of China." It is also known that although Tibet is recognized by all countries in the world (including Britain) as part of China, the passport of the Tibetan trade delegation that visited Europe and the United States last year was not obtained from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Chinese government, but from the British government in Hong Kong.

Reasons for the Mutiny of the Chongqing Warship; Air Force Bombing and Recognition of Contributing Personnel 40

[Our Newspaper, Nanjing, 21st] The most deadly bomb that destroyed the Chongqing warship was dropped on the 18th by bombadier Wen Guangqin from the aircraft. This bomb severely damaged the ship, rendering it immobile. The B-24 aircraft carrying the bombardier on this mission was piloted by Major Yang Yongtao. More aircraft went on missions on the 19th, and all the bombs dropped exploded on the ship, with the furthest being within 50 meters of the ship. On this day, Wen Guangqin again dropped a fatal bomb from Yang Yongtao's plane, hitting the ship's tail oil depot, causing the entire ship to catch fire. On the 19th, other planes piloted by Huang Feida, Wang Taiyun, and Li Jianlun also hit the ship with bombs, while Wang Yongxi and Ji Ren, through bombing, hit parts of the ship's surface. These two groups of crew members, totaling six people, have been identified as figures who made special contributions. During the three days of bombing, the anti-aircraft fire was very intense on the 18th and 19th, and the height of the shells exceeded the position of the aircraft. As a result, the oil pipe of the third engine of the plane piloted by Wang Dingji was broken by shrapnel, which hindered flight, but Wang Dingji still managed to fly the plane back and safely land at the base. Others, such as Liu Xirui and Hou Yuan, went to bomb for three days, and pilots such as Jin Zhineng, Yu Keying, and Song Tianxin all calmly went back and forth, accomplishing their missions. It was truly the most successful group action of the squadron. In this battle to bomb the Chongqing, the B-25 aircraft of the Ninth Squadron also flew to participate in the bombing. When the C-47 transport plane went to scout for the first time, it was heavily attacked by ground artillery fire. The pilots Jiang Fukao and Wang Jindu were captivated by the scenery above Huludao, and their flight was so low and close to the Chongqing before returning. [Our Newspaper, Nanjing, 21st] Although the reasons for the betrayal of the Chongqing warship are very complex, according to insiders familiar with the navy, the main reasons are nothing more than: (1) As everyone knows, the salaries of officers and soldiers are too low, and the life of the officers and soldiers of the ship during their internship in England is worlds apart from their life after returning home. (2) Among the officers and soldiers of the navy, there are always divisions of the Mawei faction, the Beiyang faction, and the Qingdao faction, and the internal struggles are extremely fierce. When Chen Shaokuan was in charge of the Naval Headquarters, the naval orders were almost all monopolized by the people of the Mawei faction. After Gui Yongqing took office, he broke this regional concept in many ways, which was dissatisfactory to the people of the Fujian faction. Deng Zhaoxiang, the former captain of the Chongqing warship, belonged to the Mawei faction, while the new captain (probationary captain) Lu Dongge (from Hebei) belonged to the Beiyang faction. When the Naval Headquarters announced Lu's succession to Deng as the captain of the Chongqing warship, it was met with dissatisfaction from Deng and some Mawei faction figures on the ship. Therefore, the departure of the Chongqing warship, with personnel friction, should be its most important factor. (3) Up to now, the materials obtained by the relevant parties indicate that there were only four or five communist agents lurking on the ship who were engaged in instigating betrayal before the ship's departure. The judgment is that these few people were able to force the ship to sail north by taking advantage of Captain Deng's knowledge that he was being transferred and his dissatisfaction with the Naval Headquarters, inciting Deng to issue a false order and sail north directly. After all, the captain is the highest person in charge of a ship, and all orders must be obeyed unconditionally. According to the relevant parties, the new captain Lu Dongge had been credited for his command of a naval unit in the battles of Yingkou and Huludao in the past. When the Naval Headquarters learned that the ship had sailed north on its own and had not sailed towards Taiwan, it still believed that it might be Captain Deng who had sailed the ship north, telling Probationary Captain Lu to "learn by doing." Later, after the Naval Headquarters ordered Captain Deng to sail south by radio and he did not comply, it became aware of the mutiny.

[Our Newspaper, Taipei, 21st] Hundreds of students from National Taiwan University and Taiwan Normal University gathered in front of the City Police Headquarters at about 11 a.m. on the 21st to protest the detention and abuse of two National Taiwan University students by the Huashan Police Station of the City Police Department at 10 p.m. on the 20th for riding a bicycle together. Because the two National Taiwan University students did not speak the local language, they had an argument with the police officers when they were interfered with, which led to them being beaten and abused. They were transferred to the Fourth Branch overnight by the police station. During the trip, one of the students found an opportunity to escape and returned to school to gather more than a hundred classmates. At about 3 a.m. before dawn, they rushed to the Fourth Branch. At that time, there were many people and things were mixed up, and the furniture and sundries in the branch were quite damaged. When the headquarters heard the news, it sent an inspector to mediate. Unexpectedly, the inspector and the director of the Fourth Branch were invited by the students to the school for negotiations. The situation did not subside. This morning, the National Taiwan University students and Taiwan Normal University jointly proposed to Director Liu Jianlie of the headquarters to punish the police officers who caused the incident, compensate for medical expenses, and publish an apology in the newspaper. After all the demands were met, they returned to school. The inspector and the director of the branch who were invited to National Taiwan University were also picked up by the police station.

The Western Districts of Berlin Unify the Currency System; The Soviet Union Adopts Countermeasures; Stricter Blockade Fails to Stop Large Amounts of Deutschmark from Entering 53

[Reuters, Berlin, 21st] Marshal Sokolovsky, commander-in-chief of the Soviet forces in Germany, ordered a strict blockade around the western districts of Berlin this morning to prevent residents of West Berlin from transporting large amounts of East German Marks, which had been discontinued in the Ding district, into the eastern district. However, a large amount still slipped in, and people were rushing to buy goods in the eastern district stores.

Observers predict that the Ding district authorities' order to ban East German Marks will intensify the Cold War between the East and West. The Berlin West District City Council held a meeting in a tense atmosphere today. While welcoming this measure by the Western authorities, they expressed concern about the countermeasures that the Soviet authorities might take. Berlin West District Mayor Reuter stated at a press conference that the measures taken by the Dingfang authorities were in line with our opinions. The German industry in West Berlin can now get rid of the chaos of the two currencies and obtain real assistance.

The Plan to Merge Berlin into West Germany is Gradually Being Realized

Commanders Bourne and Hollar of the British and American Berlin jointly held a press conference, saying that the new measures of the currency system in Ding Berlin had been under consideration for a long time, and this move was tantamount to completely absorbing the currency system of the West Berlin district into the West German currency system. The merger of Berlin into Ding Germany is gradually being realized. Hollar also said that the Soviet authorities can at most take blockade measures, but the Allied authorities have overcome the difficulties caused by the blockade. He thinks that the Soviet side cannot take more cruel retaliatory actions for the time being.

Deliberately Overthrowing Tito's Regime; The Soviet Union Adopts a Policy of Division; Large Troop Movements on the Southern Border are Said to Be Psychological Warfare 57

[United Press, London, 20th] The British Balkans are skeptical of reports of troop movements in Yugoslavia's neighboring countries, believing it to be "psychological warfare." They believe that the Kremlin will launch an anti-Tito movement within Yugoslavia.

Communist International leaders have never recognized Yugoslavia as a simple country in normal events. Yugoslavia is expected to eventually split into different ethnic countries, such as Croatia, Serbia, Macedonia, and Montenegro. From the end of the war until the Stalin-Tito conflict began, the key to the Soviet Union's policy was to form a federal Yugoslav state. The main storm within Yugoslavia in the future will be (1) Macedonia, which has one million residents opposed to Tito, and Communist Party members in Greece and Albania. The supporters of the Communist International in Macedonia advocate the establishment of an independent Macedonian state. (2) Montenegro, which has 300,000 residents, is the province with the most traditional pro-Soviet sentiment in Yugoslavia. How to Win World Peace 67

— Biao

Unintentionally, today's world is a world dominated by the United States and the Soviet Union, or, in short, a bipolar world. At the same time, the two powers are playing distinctly different tunes. The Soviet Union has been infiltrating its political influence in Europe and Asia, while the Western European democratic bloc of countries, with the support of the United States, is also busy resisting. In this situation, one cannot help but wonder whether the life of the United Nations will end in the competition between the two powers, followed by the outbreak of World War III.

Since neither of the two powers currently has the strength to control the entire world, and the Soviet Union is currently entitled to recover the losses suffered during the war, it will not easily provoke a direct conflict with democratic countries. Although people are well aware that the United States surpasses any other country in military strength, possessing atomic bombs and strong land and sea forces, and backed by a large industrial capacity, it is unlikely to provoke a devastating war against public opinion, at least under the current democratic system.

Although Soviet leaders have different opinions on the future peace of the world, they have a firm and unchanging view that capitalism itself has an inherent error factor. Therefore, before the atomic bomb is manufactured, the Soviet Union will patiently wait for the demise of capitalism, except for waiting for opportunities.

However, a small number of extremists believe that the two ideologies have no reason to coexist and will eventually conflict. Instead of waiting until atomic bombs have all been manufactured before engaging in war, it is better to let it break out sooner, which can be resolved quickly and avoid a prolonged war that causes misery to the people. Obviously, this view is extremely wrong. The reasons can be summarized into roughly three points:

(1) Modern warfare relies not only on superior weapons to win, but also on possessing a large number of well-trained troops and rapid mobilization as a supplement to achieve the goal. With the advancement of modern warfare weapons, the key to victory lies in the two conditions of "blitzkrieg" and "surprise." The United States, which possesses atomic bombs, lacks both. (2) If the United States were to launch a war, it would inevitably have to seek a final victory. However, in the brutal process of modern warfare, both enemies and friends would inevitably be destroyed. The result would be nothing more than turning the two powers into one power, and this single-power world is not what the United States and the Soviet Union want. Therefore, launching World War III is meaningless. (3) If we were to use the power of atomic bombs to force the enemy to surrender, then in future international occasions, it would be difficult for us to get friendly countries to get along in mutual trust. The world after that would still be in an unstable state of mutual suspicion. If a country wins twice with atomic bombs, it will be difficult to win over friendly countries with mutual trust to jointly maintain world peace.

Based on the above reasons, stopping war with war is by no means a good strategy for seeking peace, unless there is a particularly provocative event between the two countries, or one party has a challenging behavior. We believe that world peace can still be achieved if properly managed. If the United States holds a view that the current state of mutual calm is only a temporary truce, and that once the opportunity matures, we will face a well-prepared and powerful enemy, then future peace will be difficult to sustain.

The current problem is that if the United States tries to maintain world peace solely by strengthening its military force, then the United States' preparations for war will be enough to stimulate the Soviet Union's preparations for war. If the United States has atomic bombs, the Soviet Union can also research and manufacture them. Such unlimited expansion of military power will result in an unprecedented and devastating war. In this war, both sides will use the latest weapons against each other, using long-range aircraft to bomb each other, turning prosperous cities into ruins in an instant. Even if victory is achieved, national strength and culture cannot be restored in a short period of time. As a result, the powers after the war will actually be inferior to underdeveloped countries that have not participated in the war, and will no longer be first-class powers that dominate the world.

The reasons why the United States was fortunate enough to win the past two world wars were nothing more than the following two points: (1) The United States was able to smoothly convert peacetime industries into wartime industries; (2) It used Western European allies as a forward base and the distance of the Atlantic Ocean to win sufficient time for mobilization and preparation.

However, in future atomic warfare, it will be extremely difficult to obtain the time to change industries. At the same time, the Western European powers are no longer as capable as before, and the distance of the ocean cannot be used as a security barrier. Unless the United States converts wartime industries before the outbreak of war, the United States' fighting power is expected to be far less than before. In the course of fierce war, if atomic bombs are used as weapons, regardless of the amount, the lives and property of both sides will be destroyed, and everyone will perish together.

Since war is not a blessing for either side, and peace is what the world hopes for, to win peace, the international order must first be balanced. So-called balancing means that the Soviet Union and Western European democratic countries can coexist and work for common interests, thereby reducing conflicts and animosity between the two powers.

If there are only the United States and the Soviet Union in the world, the future of peace will be worrying. It will be difficult for the two countries to maintain a balance. Fortunately, in addition to the two powers, there are many independent countries with vast resources and a large population, which can be intermediaries for collective security. If these intermediaries strengthen their power, they can become a powerful force for maintaining world peace and creating a balanced international order.

If the many intermediary countries are weak and chaotic, then these weak and chaotic countries can easily become satellite states of any one power, and the consequence will be that the balance of the world will be lost, and world turmoil will be unavoidable. On the other hand, if the politics of the intermediary countries can be stable, the economy can be revived, and they are not controlled by any one power, then not only can the two powers have room for buffer, but world peace can also be sustained as a result.

There are three ways to win international peace: (1) The United States establishes a powerful and unparalleled military force to force all countries to abide by their posts and jointly maintain international peace; (2) The United States and the Soviet Union directly conclude a treaty without other relations to implement an international non-interference policy; (3) Assist intermediary countries in establishing a Eurasian balanced system, so that different ideologies can coexist in the world, recognizing the existence of struggle, and using methods other than war to resolve disputes between the two countries.

We believe that the first method, in addition to deliberately building a strong military force, cannot achieve international coexistence, but only stimulates the determination of another power to expand its military. Using military force to maintain peace, peace will not be permanent, so seeking peace with military force is a dream.

The second method, in which the United States and the Soviet Union conclude a treaty alone and coexist with other friendly countries in a non-interfering manner, would certainly pose no problem for world peace if it could be realized. However, judging from the current situation, there are at least the following two difficulties: (1) Under the current circumstances, the United States and the Soviet Union still suspect each other, and in the past, they have held different views and funded different hostile policies of intermediary countries. Under these circumstances, even if a treaty is concluded, is it not dead in name only, and what is the use? (2) Among the two powers, there are still many countries with political corruption and economic disorder, and it is almost hopeless to reform on their own. If we sit idly by and allow the source of chaos to grow, it will eventually affect world peace. At this time, foreign aid is naturally needed. If, under the non-interference treaty between the United States and the Soviet Union, these countries become poor and weak and unable to extricate themselves, and the weak are placed next to strong neighbors, war will inevitably occur, and peace will become a bubble.

The third method is to recognize the existence of the struggle between the two systems and to hope that this struggle exists in a peaceful state. This peaceful struggle is the so-called "cold war." The Cold War includes political and economic pressure on each other, ideological and psychological offensives, and other strategies such as using propaganda and infiltration to achieve the goal of its superiority. It is generally believed that the danger of the Cold War is nothing more than that the Cold War may provoke a hot war in the long run, but this is actually impossible. It must be understood that the Cold War was initiated because the Cold War initiator avoided a hot war.

In general, Cold War initiators must have many goals to be achieved in the Cold War, but it all depends on the situation. If they encounter resistance in the Cold War that is unexpected, they will stop after receiving a slight harvest. If the progress is smoother, they will intensify and demand more and bigger goals.

The reason why the Cold War is better than the Hot War is not only that the method is peaceful, but that it is possible to stop at the slightest benefit once it encounters resistance. However, once a Hot War is launched, it cannot be compromised halfway until victory or defeat is clear. Because of the brutality of the Hot War, no one dares to try it lightly, so there is a peaceful Cold War. Since differences between the two powers are inevitable, the Cold War cannot be eliminated. In the Cold War, the United States is using its huge economic power and solid resources to help the economic recovery of intermediary countries, so that they can become independent and prosperous, and be a stabilizing force for lasting world peace. However, the economic power of the United States is not inexhaustible, and the total wealth of the intermediary countries is no longer a force to be reckoned with. Therefore, how to effectively use this huge power is the US's peaceful Cold War strategy. The success or failure of the Cold War strategy is the success or failure of world peace. The Soviet Union is now using its only weapon to wage the Cold War, namely, thought and ideology. In the past, Gu Lian used this weapon to infiltrate the Balkans, Hungary, Greece, and the Near East, gaining widespread support.

In short, in order to win the support of intermediary countries, it is necessary not to force intermediary countries to adopt similar political and economic systems. The so-called international coexistence must be built on accommodating dissent, so that any country has a government that suits its own national conditions and resolves its own national destiny. In addition, international ideological exchanges, increased diplomatic relations, and treaty agreements can increase mutual understanding and understanding, so that countries with different systems can still coexist in a peaceful environment. (Abridged translation of an article from the American Yale Review, "Peace Strategy")

The Third Ration of Rice This Month Will Be Replaced by Flour; Each Certificate Gets Five Jin at a Fixed Price of 2,100 Yuan; Sufficient Grain Reserves Mean White Rice Will Still Be Rationed Next Month 68

[Reported by this newspaper] Mayor Wu reported to newspaper reporters in the city government office at 5 pm yesterday that the third ration of rice this month would be replaced by flour across the board. Sales are scheduled to begin today (22nd) and end on March 31st. All citizens of this city can purchase five jin of American flour from the designated rice shops in their respective districts with the third section of their March ration certificate at a price of 2,100 gold yuan. Those with key ration certificates can purchase it for 1,600 gold yuan. The flour being rationed this time is processed in the United States, and its quality is superior to the previously rationed flour.

Mayor Wu then reported that the reason for replacing rice with flour was to help the American side clear out their inventory. The flour was originally intended to be transported to North China, but due to the disruption of transportation, it could not be transported. If it was not used in time, it was feared that it would be damaged over time. After the American side requested assistance, Mayor Wu believed that the city should accept the request, so he decided to replace the household rice with American flour across the board. Wu also hoped that citizens would not doubt the source of rice, as the city has sufficient rice reserves and the flour could be rationed in full this period. Next time onwards, white rice will continue to be rationed. In addition, the household rice rationing work in this city can definitely continue to be held after April. It will be decided again after the US Congress passes it in July.

Following the Case of the Corpse in the Box, Another Horrific Blood Case; Dismembered Male Corpse Found Near Qi Lu Villa on Jinyi Road; Whereabouts of Head and Hands Still Under Investigation 73

[Reported by this newspaper] A horrific and bizarre case of a corpse dismembered into seven pieces in a box occurred at the North Railway Station in this city one afternoon. It shocked the society at that time. It has been more than two weeks since then, and the case has not yet been solved. Unexpectedly, at about 7:30 yesterday morning, another case of a male corpse dismembered into countless pieces was found near the back door of Qi Lu Villa on Jinyi Road in Shanghai West, hidden in yellow tarpaulin packages and travel bags. It can be said that it is not an isolated incident. The details are recorded below:

At about 7:30 yesterday morning, Li Changjiu, who was watching the public cemetery, discovered a yellow tarpaulin package shaped like luggage outside the back door of Qi Lu Villa (i.e., Shandong Fellow Association) at No. 465, the intersection of Jinyi Road and Xieshi Road. It was tied with white hemp rope. Then, a large travel bag was found in the nearby creek. Immediately moved by curiosity, he walked to the river bank and bowed his head to open the zipper of the travel bag. He saw many pieces that looked like pig knuckles. Upon closer inspection, they were not meat. Li was greatly suspicious and rushed to report to the accounting room of the Fellow Association, who reported it to the Changshu Road Police Station. The criminal section chief Chen Fenglin was dispatched, leading police officer Zhu Yunlin to investigate. The tarpaulin package was opened again, and it was found to be a dismembered body. It was determined to be a serious assassination case. Section Chief Chen telegraphed the branch director Cheng Yikuan, who personally led the deputy branch director Wang Sizu, the section chief, and several plainclothes police officers to the scene to investigate. It was found that the flesh in the travel bag was slightly discolored due to prolonged immersion in water, while the tarpaulin package contained two packages of limbs, a total of thirty-two pieces. Branch Director Cheng immediately reported to the headquarters and dispatched forensic doctor Dr. Liang Hanfen, together with detectives and police officers from the photography room Fang Meifa, etc., who arrived at the scene one after another.

It Is Presumed That the Deceased Was Definitely Not a Laborer

After repeated examinations by Dr. Liang, it was recorded that one part was chopped with a knife and the other part was sawed off. It was also determined that the dismemberment was after the person was killed. The body had no scars all over, and the cut of the bones and muscles was very neat. It was speculated that the deceased was about thirty-one or two years old, weighed about 160 pounds or more, and was about five feet and four inches tall. It was also inferred from the heels that this person was definitely not a laborer, and it was determined that the death period was no more than two days. The dismembered body includes (1) a section of neck meat, (2) a piece of bone under the neck, (3) a piece in the middle of the back, (4) a piece of hip under the waist, (5) a section of the upper left back, (6) two sections of the right forearm, (7) one section each of the upper part of the left and right thighs, (8) one section each of the center of the left and right knees, (9) one section each of the left and right calves, (10) five pieces of the left and right ankles, (11) one heart, (12) one-quarter of the kidney thief, (13) two pieces of the chest breasts, (14) ten pieces of broken muscles. The missing parts include the head, the left and right eyebrows, the front chest bone, the diaphragm, the internal organs, the upper half of the buttocks, the right front chest, the left and right palms, fingers, one section of the thigh, the left and right toes, half a kidney, and the genitals.

Lead Printed Strips in the Sleeves of a Woman's Jacket

The items placed under the body parts include a woman's cheongsam cotton wool strip, four silk cotton tires of children's open crotch pants, a square cotton tire, a tattered mattress cotton wool strip, a blue-faced and green-bottom cotton woman's short jacket, and a copy of the Ta Kung Pao dated December 14, 1948. A piece of paper with lead-printed characters of No. 6 was placed in the sleeve of the woman's short jacket, which reads "If people have hatred for me, it can be forgotten and not thought of." The paper strip is about one and a half inches long and about three inches wide. In addition, it rained all day the day before yesterday, and it did not stop until midnight, while the hemp rope on the oil bag was still dry. Therefore, it is predicted that the murderer moved the body to the place around five or six o'clock in the morning. After the forensic doctor examined it, the police officers transported the two packages of body parts to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall. At the same time, the Tan Branch Bureau issued an arrest warrant for the fleeing murderer to bring him to justice.

The record shows that the defendant Zhao Changgeng was addicted to gambling and often asked his brother for loans, but he was not satisfied and had harbored resentment for a long time. At midnight on the 4th of last month, Changgeng took advantage of his brother Jinpei being asleep at home, sneaked into the bedroom with a knife, and stabbed his brother several times. Jinpei cried for help in pain and was rushed to the hospital by his family for treatment. He recovered his health. Upon hearing the news, the police station arrested Changgeng and transferred him to the district prosecutor's office for investigation and prosecution.

Surging and Sinking Speculative Mania: A Typical Figure – Throwing Gold, Lending Money, Sometimes Earning, Sometimes Losing, Ultimately Facing Great Defeat 77

[Special Report from Our Newspaper] Little Zhang, it is unknown where he is from. His colleagues in the office only knew that he was a long-time resident of Nanjing and had just received a bachelor's degree in economics from a prestigious university in Nanjing half a year ago. His uncle was the deputy manager of the business department of a powerful bank in Shanghai. With this connection, Little Zhang became an investigation specialist in the department managed by his uncle. Little Zhang never understood the Shanghai style of his colleagues in the office. Seeing them set aside their official duties to inquire about the market prices of gold, paper money, and stocks, he thought, "These guys really deserve to die, just taking money and not working. I must set an example for them!"

But a month or two passed, and Little Zhang mixed in the office and ran around outside. His stubborn Beijing style finally began to waver. Moreover, the money he received based on the cost of living index bought less and less each month. He thought that in this day and age, he should use his business acumen. With the economic theories he learned at the university, as well as his contacts and social interactions, he was not afraid of not being able to win in the business world. Having made up his mind, Little Zhang found several gold speculation firms through introductions. He only needed to pay two taels of margin to trade futures contracts of ten taels per bar.

Receiving News, Selling Two Bars

That night, Little Zhang somehow received absolutely accurate news that the Central Bank, in order to contract the currency supply to cooperate with the implementation of the new financial plan, had decided to continuously sell large quantities of gold, silver dollars, foreign exchange transfer certificates, cotton yarn, sugar, and so on. He thought that since the announcement of the new financial plan, prices had already risen several times and seemed to have reached a saturation point. The market's money supply had approached the seven-corner level. According to the quantity theory of money, the general price level is directly proportional to the quantity of currency and its velocity of circulation. Therefore, the price of gold would definitely fall in the following days. Tomorrow, he would find the right market price to sell short and borrow money, which would be a good deal.

The next morning, Little Zhang signed in at the office and sneaked out under the pretext of conducting an investigation. He arrived at the gold firm. There were still ten minutes before the market opened, but the unofficial gold market was still hovering at a high level. At 9:30 AM, the market opened at a high of 3.35 million, and Little Zhang, feeling that he had found the right opportunity, sold two bars. He mortgaged four small gold bars borrowed from his colleague Old Ma. The 6.7 million yuan he earned from selling short was credited to his account by the gold firm at an interest rate of seven corners.

Gold Becomes Cheap, Interest Rates High: Double Income

Little Zhang's dream did not fail. On the day he sold short, the gold market initially hovered at a high level. Just as the market was evening out near noon, news suddenly came that the Central Bank was selling to the market through a certain gold firm, in lots of ten or twenty bars. The market price fell by more than ten levels in a quarter of an hour, eventually closing at 2.97 million. Little Zhang was overjoyed with his initial victory. He boasted to his colleagues, who praised him for having a "promising start." Little Zhang, following the trend, said, "Watch me make a promising start for two more days!"

Indeed, in the following two days, the Central Bank not only sold gold in the gold market but also sold yarn, sugar, and foreign exchange transfer certificates. All market prices were suppressed. The money supply was tightened to an unprecedented level, and the daily interest rate exceeded one yuan. On the fourth day after Little Zhang sold gold, he thought he had earned enough and decided to cover his position. Calculating his gains, he had earned seven corners of interest per day, one yuan and one corner of interest in two days, plus the difference between selling high and buying low, for a total profit of more than 2.3 million gold yuan. He bought back seven taels of gold at the market price of 3.3 million on that day, with some gold yuan still left over. What a great profit, how could it not make everyone in the office envious? However, Little Zhang still felt that he had not earned enough. Because after he covered his position, the market price continued to hover for two days, and the daily interest rate remained at seven or eight corners.

After this, Little Zhang's interest in and confidence in speculating in the gold market suddenly increased. He told people that the first time was just a small try, a little "promising start," and that the real skill was yet to come. Sure enough, in the subsequent rounds of buying and selling, Little Zhang was almost always successful, at most only having the problem of earning enough versus not earning enough.

Receiving News Again, Selling Ten Bars

One day, Little Zhang again received inside information from some well-informed source that the authorities were going to sell off large quantities. Seeing that the money supply had been loose and excessive for a while, as long as there was news of the authorities selling off large quantities, the money supply would inevitably tighten, and the daily interest rate would rise. Having made up his mind, he decided to sell short ten bars in one go.

The next morning, the gold market opened at 3.75 million, and the daily interest rate was about six corners. Within half an hour, the price of gold actually rose to the four million mark due to the continued loose money supply. When would he sell if not now? This time, Little Zhang resolutely sold short ten bars, immediately paying the margin for two bars. However, this time, because the money supply was loose, and rumors spread in the market that the authorities had a large remittance outflow, the money supply flooded, and the daily interest rate opened low, only about five corners.

Price Plunges, Loses Everything

Little Zhang told everyone he met: "The 'promising start' of this transaction is yet to come. Just wait and see." He planned to hold on for three days. On the first day, not only did the price of gold exceed the four million mark in the morning, but the next day's trading price rose to over 4.5 million. On the second day, the authorities had no news of selling anything, but remittances continued to flow in from other cities, the money supply remained loose, and the daily interest rate plummeted to only four and a half corners. The price of gold rose even further to 4.8 million. On the third day, the trend remained the same. Little Zhang was determined to hold on to the end, but unexpectedly, on the fourth day, the authorities suddenly released a large amount of "ice eggs" (frozen goods) worth tens of billions, the market's money supply completely flooded, and the price of gold broke through the five million mark, soaring to 5.35 million. Little Zhang, who had always been confident, turned pale. His previous gains, after calculation, not only returned everything, but also resulted in a loss of five or six taels. The two taels of margin paid to the gold firm now only had one or two taels left. Old Min, the gold firm owner, was opportunistic. Seeing that Little Zhang's margin was insufficient, he not only demanded additional margin but also advised Little Zhang to cover his position and settle the account as soon as possible! In this situation of being besieged on all sides, Little Zhang finally had no choice but to painfully close his position.

Fantasy of Getting Rich Disappears; Vows Never to Speculate Again

This was a "lost weekend." On the train back to Nanjing, Little Zhang carefully calculated the net loss of this final battle. Not only did it swallow up all his previous speculative gains, but it also dragged him into a debt of five taels to his colleagues. There was no choice but to go home and beg his wife for some of her few pieces of jewelry. He stared blankly at the fleeting suburban scenery outside the train window, and the beautiful fantasy he had envisioned was just as fleeting as the scenery: he couldn't help but grind his teeth and complain: "These damn 'ice eggs,' damn financial authorities!" He vowed that after this lesson, he would wash his hands and never speculate again!

Barber Shop Prices Divided into Five Grades and Ten Levels; Proposed Base Numbers Seem Too High; Social Affairs Bureau Instructs to Wait for Meeting to Discuss 83

[News from Our Newspaper] The issue of setting the base numbers for barber shop prices and multiplying them by the cost of living index has not yet been resolved. The Barber Shop Trade Association has already submitted a list of base numbers to the Social Affairs Bureau. Several standing directors and directors of the association went to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday afternoon and jointly studied the matter with Section Chief Xi of the Social Affairs Bureau. They proposed that barber shops should be divided into five grades and ten levels. The special grade was 1.7 yuan before the war (multiplied by 2.5, the same below), and the current proposed base number is 4.25 yuan. The special grade deputy was 1.3 yuan before the war, and the current proposed base number is 3.25 yuan. The Grade A positive was 1 yuan before the war, and the current proposed base number is 2.5 yuan. The Grade A deputy was 8 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 2 yuan. The Grade B positive was 6.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 2.625 yuan. The Grade B deputy was 5.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 1.225 yuan. The Grade C positive was 4.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 1.125 yuan. The Grade C deputy was 3.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 8.75 yuan. The Grade D positive was 2.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 6.25 yuan. The Grade D deputy was 1.5 jiao before the war, and the current proposed base number is 3.75 yuan. They stated that due to increased water and electricity costs and huge expenses, it would not be enough to maintain if the prices were doubled according to the pre-war prices and multiplied by the cost of living index, as approved by the Municipal Council. Therefore, they slightly increased the prices by referring to the regulations of the hotel industry, which stipulate that pre-war room rates should be increased by 2.2 times, and calculated them at 2.5 times. For example, if the base number of Grade A positive is 2.5 yuan, multiplying it by the 1339.36 times on the 15th of this month would result in a charge of 3348.4 yuan per haircut. The Social Affairs Bureau believes that the set base numbers are too high and is concerned that it will cause resentment among citizens. It instructed the representatives to go back first and wait for the Social Affairs Bureau to review the matter in detail before convening another meeting for discussion.

Set Price of Regular Meal; Adjusted with Rice Price; Maximum of 1,500 Yuan; To Be Implemented After Approval by the Municipal Government 87

[News from Our Newspaper] Due to drastic price fluctuations, the price of regular meals has also risen sharply. In order to standardize the price of regular meals, the Social Affairs Bureau invited representatives from the Municipal Council, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, General Labor Union, Finance Bureau, Police Bureau, and Restaurant Trade Association yesterday afternoon to discuss the matter. It was decided that regular meals should be divided into three grades: A, B, and C. Grade A will use 2.5 sheng of white japonica rice, Grade B will use 2 sheng of white japonica rice, and Grade C will use 1.5 sheng of white japonica rice. If white japonica rice is calculated at 60,000 yuan per dan, a Grade A regular meal will cost 1,500 yuan, a Grade B regular meal will cost 1,200 yuan, and a Grade C regular meal will cost 900 yuan. In the future, the price of regular meals will be adjusted according to the rise and fall of rice prices. The plan will be submitted to the Municipal Government for approval before implementation.

Statistics on Rice Sales in City Rice Shops; Monthly Total Demand is 1.1 Million Shi; Not Including Restaurants and Factories that Purchase from Production Areas 95

[News from Our Newspaper] The Shanghai Municipal Government plans to store three months of grain. The Social Affairs Bureau, Civil Food Allocation Office, and Emergency Purchase and Storage Committee have been conducting separate investigations into the monthly grain demand and existing reserves. It is reported that they have made progress. According to the person in charge of the Social Affairs Bureau, based on the sales reports of more than 2,200 rice shops in the city over the past three months, the average monthly sale of rice is more than 580,000 shi. In addition, the Civil Food Allocation Office sold approximately 520,000 shi of household rice in February (including the converted sales of flour). The total monthly sales of rice in the city are more than 1.1 million shi. The following have not yet been determined: (1) The above figures are only the monthly sales volume and not the actual consumption volume. (2) Many restaurants, hotels, schools, and factories purchase rice directly from nearby production areas, which is not included. (3) The report on rice reserves in Shanghai is incomplete. A final decision will be made at a joint meeting of the Social Affairs Bureau, Civil Food Allocation Office, and Emergency Purchase and Storage Committee in the Broadway Mansion on the 26th of this month.

Wuxi Love Triangle Murder Retrial: Philandering Military Officer Cannot Escape Death 99

[Report from our Wuxi correspondent on the 20th] Zhang Jiming, the perpetrator of the sensational "Love Triangle Murder" in Wuxi, was apprehended in Shanghai by the Investigation Team. After being handed over to the City Defense Headquarters, he underwent multiple interrogations by the Military Tribunal. Due to conclusive evidence, he was sentenced to death according to the law. The sentence was submitted to the First Pacification District Headquarters and then to the Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou Garrison Headquarters for review. However, orders were subsequently issued for a retrial with additional witnesses. On the afternoon of the 19th, the City Defense Headquarters Military Tribunal complied by summoning witnesses Zhang Yuting, Zhang Xiaohei, Xu Arong, Chen Chengshi, Zhang Jinxiang, as well as Wu Wenhua, the director of Dahua Hospital, and Li Zhongtang, the director of Hongen Hospital, for questioning. Military Judge Chen Shimin presided over the hearing.

Shouting "Ji Ming Killed Me" Before Death

According to Zhang Yuting, 50 years old, from Hebei, an opera performer residing at the Zhongdong Theater, and the adoptive father of the deceased couple Zhao Qingsheng and Zhang Yuyan, at the time of the incident, I had already fallen asleep. Suddenly, I heard the sound of gunfire. Someone woke me up, and as I was getting dressed, Qingsheng suddenly pressed his right waist and crawled into the room, shouting, "Dad, Zhang Jiming shot me!" He then collapsed on the ground. Later, I entered Wang Yan's room, where she had already been shot dead in bed. Because I heard that Ji Ming had a gun, I dared not pursue him. I immediately sent the injured man to Hongen Hospital and reported the incident to the Investigation Team. Previously, Ji Ming had sent me a threatening letter. Then, Zhang Xiaohei, 14 years old, an opera performer who lived in the same room with Yuyan and Qingsheng, testified that they two slept in the same bed, I slept under the table. At the time of the incident, I heard Yuyan shout in my sleep, "Dad, Zhang Jiming shot me!" I was immediately startled awake. Looking up, I saw Zhang Jiming holding a bright silver pistol, pointing it at my sister Yuyan. The second shout did not sound like a human voice, but like a ghostly wail. I was so frightened that I dared not look again. Then I heard another gunshot, and Ji Ming fled. He pointed to the pistol presented in court, claiming that it was the same pistol. Following this, Chen Chengshi, Yuting's wife's younger sister, who also lived at the Dongxin Hotel, gave a statement consistent with the statements of Yuting and Xiaohei.

The Murder Scene Witnessed by a Tea Boy

Furthermore, Wu Wenhua, the director of Dahua Hospital, testified that he did not know Zhang Jiming. Zhao Qingsheng was sent to the hospital for treatment at 6:00 AM on January 25, 1938. He was sent over after being treated at Hongen Hospital. He was sent to the operating room without registering. When asked, he said he was shot. After the wound was bandaged, he was asked again, and Zhao's expression was extremely resentful, "gritting his teeth and shouting, 'That Zhang kid!'" Then, Li Zhongtang, the director of Hongen Hospital, testified that Zhang Yuting sent Zhao Qingsheng to the hospital for treatment in a rickshaw around 4:00 AM. Zhao said, "Dad, quickly go and arrest Zhang Jiming." I examined him and found two bullet wounds in each of his thighs and one in his abdomen, with four holes on his legs. I determined that he had been shot two or one times. Subsequently, Xu Arong testified. Xu was a tea boy at the Dongxin Hotel. He said he did not know Zhang Jiming. I am here today to testify, and I will definitely tell the truth. The two actors Zhao and Zhang lived in room 12 of the Dongxin Hotel. I know all about how they were shot dead. He then described how Zhang Jiming entered the hotel late at night during curfew, his appearance, what clothes he was wearing, and how he left after the incident. Finally, he firmly stated that the two actors were killed with the pistol presented in court.

Three Identifications, Difficult to Deny

One of the witnesses, Zhang Jinxiang, was presented by the perpetrator Zhang Jiming. According to his testimony, he is 40 years old, from Guangdong, resides in Nanjing, runs a theater, and is friends with Ji Ming. Around December of the lunar calendar, they met once at the Public Recreation Club. At that time, he told everyone, "The Cultural Troupe wants to invite Peking opera actors. I can go to Shanghai and find them." Later, I heard that he had killed someone, and I have not seen him since. Finally, Military Judge Chen summoned the suspect Zhang Jiming to the court. According to his testimony, he is from Liling, Hunan, and is a major political officer in the Capital Garrison Headquarters. He met Zhang Wangyan in the theater troupe and had a physical relationship with her. She wanted to marry me, but I didn't dare to. I only met Zhao Qingsheng once. I did not kill him. On January 26, I went from Nanjing to Shanghai, and on the 27th, I went to the Garrison Department to see Director Zhang, requesting a transfer. Meanwhile, I was in Shanghai to find actors. On the 26th, when the incident occurred, I was in Shanghai. Finally, Zhang Xiaohei and Xu Arong, who witnessed the scene, were summoned to the court again. After Military Judge Chen interrogated and identified them three times in a row, it was undoubtedly Zhang Jiming who was the principal offender in this case. The department has now submitted the results of the retrial to the First Pacification District Headquarters for review. It is widely believed that the "philandering military officer" will ultimately not escape death.

Ancient and Modern Wonders, All Rights Reserved

Hangzhou Incense Pilgrimage: Talking About Sericulture and Farming 100

— Special correspondent from our newspaper, Chu Yusheng

[Report from our Hangzhou correspondent on the 19th] Spring in Hangzhou is like a painting. The beauty of the lakes and mountains is mixed with tourists, both men and women, especially those farmers who wear blue cotton jackets and carry yellow cloth bags to burn incense and pay homage to the Buddha. They walk in groups along the embankments and shores, reflecting their shadows in the lake. How poetic and picturesque! Although we stand from a position of appreciation to view this tranquil and comfortable paradise scene, if we further penetrate the feelings of the people in the painting, there must be a lot of bitterness and everyday life. Those farmers, they come to Hangzhou not to travel and play, but to sincerely burn incense and worship Buddha, seeking happiness for the year. Therefore, in the rural areas of Jiangnan, as long as one mentions going to Hangzhou to burn incense at the Buddhist temple, everyone will put everything aside and work hard to go. In the years of peace, for the sake of peace and prosperity, for the sake of abundant silkworm cocoons, and for the sake of abundant harvests, no farmer's family would fail to send one or two people to Hangzhou to burn incense. This year's situation is obviously different. There are not as many boats from Songmuchang as in previous years, and there are only a few people carrying yellow cloth bags along the embankments and shores. I asked several old ladies, and what they told me really made us feel sad.

Last year's harvest was not very good, but the orders to collect grain and conscript soldiers were unusually urgent. The grain was harvested from the fields, threshed into rice, and carried to the town to pay taxes. The people weighing the grain would either say that the grain was wet and not accept it, or they would turn the small scale into a large scale, and if the weight was insufficient, they would have to bring more to compensate. From the township to the fields, it takes a day's journey, and the wages and food of the boatmen have to be taken care of by themselves. Some people avoid trouble, as long as they show respect to the grain collectors, they can get away with it. Look at the faces of those grain collectors, they are more fierce than the bodhisattva guarding the entrance of the City God Temple! As for soldiers, those with money and power, even if a family has five or six strong men, will not have problems. But poor families, even if they have only one son to rely on for life, will be drafted. They beg the head of the village, but the head of the village says this is a public matter. They beg the head of the district, but the head of the district says this is an order from above. After bitter pleading, they finally agree, but they must pay two or three dan of rice as a settlement fee for the conscript.

They don't know anything about agricultural loans and cooperatives. During the spring plowing season, they still have to borrow some from the powerful families to make ends meet. Several times, it was said that the officials in the town received orders from the officials in the county to investigate and inspect, and they had to be treated to big fish and big meat. They wiped their mouths and left, and the remaining debt was spread on the poor and powerless.

Their houses are still built by their ancestors, and they don't have the ability to add new homes now. The big pigs and small pigs in the pigsties are gradually decreasing. The waterwheels, plows, and hoes used for plowing are all old, and the old cattle are also weak. Their only blame is that it is destined in fate. Only by sincerely believing in the Bodhisattva can they be reborn in the next life as an official in the town, or as a person who makes a fortune, builds tall houses, adds new furniture, and fills the pigsties with pigs. Then they don't have to go to the fields to farm themselves, and they can comfortably enjoy themselves. This is the only fantasy of burning incense. This year, the rice stored at home is all gone. The incense leader everywhere asks people to come to Hangzhou to burn incense, but each person needs seven dou of rice. Seven dou of rice is not a small number in a farming family that produces food. In addition, after taking the rice out to burn incense, they don't know how to live when they come back, and they also heard that the situation is not good, so there are not as many people coming to Hangzhou to burn incense this time as in previous years.

Based on the above-mentioned accounts of these old ladies, we can already understand the situation of our countryside. The people in the cities take everything from the countryside. What about the countryside? Only giving, not receiving, let alone leaving some benefits to the countryside. Under layers of exploitation, our countryside has become extremely anemic, extremely declining, and extremely paralyzed. The countryside, under layers of constraints, their ideas are also very backward. They still have the ideas of the 19th century, wanting to be officials and make a fortune. They still ask the Bodhisattva to give comfort, happiness, and joy!

Rural education cannot be delayed any longer, giving them new production skills, giving them new knowledge, giving them new farm tools, giving them new methods!

China is still an agricultural country after all. Our true masters have been silent, enduring hardships for so many years. They are about to be paralyzed and on the verge of desperation. Truly, when the nest is overturned, there are no intact eggs. We must improve all methods of administration.

In the spring, under the quiet and tranquil atmosphere of West Lake, many poetic and picturesque scenes are left for poets and writers to chant and write about. The above-mentioned facts should also be cited as the best material for reality.

Victims of the Fire on Liyuan Road in the South City Send a Letter to the Public Asking for Righteous Support 102

Expressing Resistance to Profiteering from the Fire and the Landlords' Eviction Tactics

Dear Editor: We are a group of refugees who fled to Shanghai. Two years ago, unable to withstand the threat of the civil war's artillery fire, we came to Shanghai together. We worked hard and built some thatched sheds and plank houses on Liyuan Road to shield ourselves from the wind and rain. A family of several people, young and old, rely on manual labor to survive. Daily life is already hard enough. Unexpectedly, on the 5th of this month, another fire broke out, and more than 300 of our shacks were all reduced to ashes. The situation was like this: around 2 PM that day, a fire broke out in a shack due to careless use of the stove. The South Shanghai District Fire Brigade was immediately notified to come and put out the fire. However, the Liyuan Road area has always lacked fire hydrants. Although the firefighters were quick to work, the water supply was too far away, and the wind added to the situation. By the time the water reached the fire, the fire had already burned very fiercely. After the fire was extinguished, none of our more than 300 families were spared. When the fire broke out, we were all working outside due to the demands of life and couldn't rush back in time. Therefore, although the women managed to salvage a few household items, they were looted by a group of thugs who took advantage of the fire. Now we are cleaning up the ashes, but there is another message that is enough to make us heartbroken: the landlords are using various means, trying to reclaim the property rights, and drive us away. We ask, after such a great disaster, how can we have the strength to move elsewhere? We cry out for help in vain, and have no way to enter the earth. We have always admired your newspaper as the mouthpiece of the people, so we borrow a corner of your newspaper to reveal this, hoping that the government authorities and the public will give us righteous support. With best regards, the entire fire victims of Liyuan Road bow　March 10　Victim representatives Wang Hongfei, Xu Yongnian, Xia Guoyun, Zhang Qiaxiang, Proving the facts: Shi Shoudong, head of the 72nd Bao of Penglai District (seal)

A Faint Wind Blows Across Hong Kong 105

— Our reporter, Zijian

[Airmail report from our Hong Kong correspondent on the 18th] Two shocking events have recently occurred in the Hong Kong business community: a major firm engaged in trade between Hong Kong and Siam declared bankruptcy, owing more than two million yuan in payment for goods. A fairly large-scale weaving factory was also seized by the court due to debts of more than 200,000 yuan. Sensitive merchants have already shouted the catchphrase "economic downturn," but judging from the current situation in Hong Kong, "a faint wind has blown to Hong Kong" is indeed an indisputable fact.

According to a person in charge of a major British merchant bank in Hong Kong, the financial industry in Hong Kong is currently facing a depression that has not been seen in 40 years. The business of major banks is currently more than 30% lower than at the peak last year. In view of the shadow of the economic downturn, Chinese and foreign banks in Hong Kong have now taken various emergency measures, the most significant of which are two: (1) Increasing the margin for export bills. The imported goods in Hong Kong have now greatly exceeded the needs of the actual market, so the price of goods has fallen, even to a point lower than the margin for export bills. When the merchants cannot support themselves, the banks also suffer losses. All foreign banks have recently raised the margin for export bills from 25% to more than 50%. More restrictions are placed on importers and exporters with weak credit. In order to protect its own interests, the bank further increases the difficulties of merchants. (2) Reducing mortgage loans and stopping all risky loans. In January of this year, general property mortgages could still reach 60% of the original value, but recently it has been reduced to less than 50%, with the lowest reaching 30%. Banks seem to fear that the currently excessively high property values ​​in Hong Kong may decline significantly in the future. The number of goods mortgaged has also been greatly reduced. "Unpopular" goods are even refused mortgages. It is said that some British merchant banks have been ordered by their London headquarters to avoid pledging too many securities and stocks, and those that have expired must be paid off on time, and no extensions are allowed. This has caused a general decline in stock prices.

Due to the decline in import and export trade and the tightening of bank credit, Hong Kong merchants are now feeling great pressure. Those who cannot support themselves can only close down, and the two bankruptcies mentioned above are significant examples. According to an economic survey, Hong Kong's trade with China in the first quarter of this year has fallen to the lowest level since the war. Recently, the Guangdong provincial authorities have severely dealt with small-scale smuggling "water traders" in water and land transportation, which has also greatly reduced the business of general retailers in Hong Kong. Reflected in the market, tea houses, restaurants, and dance halls are desolate, and "sale" flags are planted all over the streets. Hong Kong's trade with Southeast Asia is also shrinking unprecedentedly due to competition from Japanese goods, and the weaving industry is particularly hit hard.

According to the Far Eastern Economic Review, there are 322 weaving factories in Hong Kong, and 132 have gone bankrupt. Of the 190 remaining, only 90 are still in operation. Other industries such as enamelware, rubber shoes, flashlights, and lanterns also feel that the market is narrowing and crises are lurking. The current expectations of Hong Kong merchants for new markets such as North China, Korea, Taiwan, and Europe can only be explained as an attempt to "find another way out" in difficult circumstances.

However, while a faint wind is blowing through the Hong Kong market, the Hong Kong government has proposed the largest budget in history for the next fiscal year, reaching a total of HK$180,019,370 (an increase of HK$31,014,363 from this year), with an average burden of about 100 yuan per resident. According to this huge budget, the Hong Kong government (at least for now) does not admit that Hong Kong has fallen into an economic downturn. The Hong Kong government's estimated revenue for the next fiscal year includes direct taxes, tobacco, alcohol, and cosmetics taxes, as well as food and beverage, lottery, and entertainment taxes, which account for more than half of the total (totaling HK$95,775,000). It can be seen that the Hong Kong government expects the market in Hong Kong to be quite prosperous in the coming year.

Compared with this year's income and expenditure, the Hong Kong government has a fiscal surplus of 24 million yuan. Adding the surplus figures for the previous two years, the surplus figure in the Hong Kong treasury is 60 million yuan. According to Hong Kong's Financial Secretary Huo Laoshi's report, "He believes that this figure is not enough for Hong Kong to get through its period of nutritional deficiency." He advocates that Hong Kong establish a large reserve fund to cope with unexpected needs. It is not known whether the so-called "unexpected needs" is an hint of a "period of economic downturn?"

The Hong Kong government explained the increase in the next fiscal year's budget, and strongly emphasized the issue of Hong Kong's security, so it requested a large amount of administrative expenses to expand the police force and establish the Hong Kong Defense Force. The Financial Secretary said: "The core of the budget is security." It is said that those directly or indirectly used for security will reach 26 million yuan. The highest authorities of the Hong Kong government also have a statement of "preparing for the worst and hoping for the best." Living on a small island, the people are worried about the invasion of the economic downturn, while the officials are worried about the security problem. This is thought provoking!

Jiangxi Cotton Production 106

— Our reporter, Liu Zao

This came from foreign lands to the Central Plains,

The sacred sound and essence are truly the source,

With clear feet and bright eyes, the seeds are spread,

The merits of cultivation and weaving illuminate the common people.

—— Emperor Qianlong's inscription on the Baoding Cultivation and Weaving Picture ——

Jiangxi's cotton production is usually only five to six million catties per year. Given the current population of 12 million, each person needs one catty of cotton per year to make clothing and bedding fillings. The existing cotton production is not even half of the required amount. Therefore, Jiangxi's annual import of cotton textiles exceeds the total value of grain exports. Looking around the countryside, how many people's clothes can cover their bodies without showing the poor image of tattered clothes!

Jiangxi's textile industry is now in its infancy. The Jiujiang Xingzhong Yarn Factory has 20,000 spindles, and the Nanchang Xinsheng Yarn Factory currently has 2,000 spindles and may add another 3,000 spindles in the short term. The two factories need about 50,000 dan of fine short-staple raw cotton annually, more than 90% of which relies on supplies from Hankou and Anqing. The green-seed American cotton produced in the alluvial layer along the Poyang Lake area, such as Pengze, only accounts for 10% of the supply to the textile industry. The cotton for clothing and bedding fillings in the countryside, in addition to a part taken from the province's production, is mostly imported from Huangmei and Wuxue in southern Hubei and the Dongting Lake area in Hunan Province. In addition, cotton textiles imported from Beijing and Shanghai, of course, also replace part of the cotton consumption.

The Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry's Cotton Production Improvement Department is coordinating the increase in cotton production nationwide.

Jiangxi is now listed as one of the provinces that are self-sufficient in cotton production. Therefore, increasing cotton production in Jiangxi is a major issue in Jiangxi's economic development. In the past two years, the promotion of cotton production has achieved considerable results through the efforts of the Northern Jiangxi Cotton Planting Guidance Office. Last year, the cotton planting in Yongxiu, Pengze, and other places was affected by the biggest flood in more than ten years, which affected the cotton harvest. However, cotton farmers' use of and confidence in the improved cotton variety - Dai-Character Cotton - has been improved. In the future, Jiangxi's cotton production will enter a stage of increased production to achieve the goal of self-sufficiency.

The results of land reclamation and experimentation by the Northern Jiangxi Cotton Field in Pengze:

American Cotton Regional Experiment

Including the main American cotton varieties introduced by former countries, the varieties selected and bred by domestic agricultural agencies, and the degraded American cotton varieties cultivated locally in the Northern Jiangxi region, a total of 18 varieties. The results of the experiment showed that the average yield of seed cotton was 165.6 catties per mu (Chinese acre). The yield of Jingzhi Cotton (207.4) catties was the highest, followed by D.P.L-14 (191.4) catties, Suining No. 75 (188.7) catties ranked third, and Huanong No. 2 (185) catties ranked fourth. The Pengze promotion species of Dai-Character Cotton ranked fifth with (178.8) catties. The Pengze degraded American cotton D531 and FOSTER 63 varieties ranked first, second, and third from the bottom with (144.8) catties, (146.1) catties, and (147.4) catties per mu, respectively. The Dai-Character Cotton has a particularly high lint percentage and its maturity period is slightly earlier than the De-Character Cotton, which is indeed a variety that can be promoted at present. Jingzhi Cotton and Suining No. 75 are early-maturing and high-yielding, grow neatly, and have a medium-to-high lint percentage, which are particularly noteworthy. Jingzhi Cotton was originally developed in the Si-Character Cotton system adapted to the cotton-growing area of the Yellow River Basin. Now it is also adapted to the cotton-growing area of the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and shows excellent results. According to people in charge of increasing cotton production in Jiangxi, this experiment is worth studying and is a very interesting result.

Northern Jiangxi Cotton by Tractor Land Reclamation (Photo by Liu Zao)

The Gold Market Opens Today: Gold Business Association Held Reopening Ceremony Yesterday; Seven Market Management Committee Members Elected 107

[Special Dispatch] The Shanghai Gold Business Association held a nominal reopening ceremony yesterday at 3 PM at the Ministry of Finance. The association gathered 63 registered and sound member firms (an increase of six firms from the previous day) for a meeting.

The long-dormant second-floor hall of the association was once again crowded. During the meeting, Xu Fusun, a leader in the industry, reported on the process of preparing for the reopening as ordered, and the 13 articles of the "Measures for Buying and Selling Gold Bullion" approved by the Ministry of Finance on March 16.

Subsequently, Zhao Zhongying, the acting chairman of the association, presided over an on-the-spot lottery to determine the order in which each member firm would use the market's telephone to contact hunger relief efforts. Finally, seven market management committee members were publicly elected. As a result, Feng Qing'an, Shao Changling, Yu Junfu, Xie Bingquan, Hong Deyu, Lu Junfu, and Chen Ruitang were elected.

The association has scheduled the resumption of market trading to begin today at 10 AM. The market will be located in the hall downstairs at the association's address at No. 4, Alley 43, North Wuxi Road. Yesterday, the telephone racks on the four walls were installed, and the intercom telephones were also properly placed. The telephone lines were expected to be installed overnight. The association has invited representatives from the Ministry of Finance, the Gold Control Bureau, the Central Bank, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to attend and provide guidance this morning.

According to Zhao Zhongying, the acting chairman of the association, who spoke to reporters, the association was ordered to resume operations first. Old members of the association can still apply for membership one after another. When the number of participating members reaches a considerable number, the association will file with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to convene a general meeting of members and re-elect directors and supervisors. The "Measures for Buying and Selling Gold Bullion" and the list of registered reopening member firms are recorded below:

Measures for Buying and Selling Gold Bullion 108

(Approved by the Ministry of Finance on March 16, 1949)

(1) Gold trading by gold firms shall be collectively conducted within the Shanghai Gold Business Association (hereinafter referred to as the "Association") by the Association's original member gold firms.

(2) The aforementioned gold firms shall be re-investigated and registered by the Association, and only those that pass the review in accordance with the articles of association shall be allowed to resume business.

(3) The buying and selling of gold shall be limited to gold bullion. Each gold firm shall negotiate prices and trade independently within the Association, with ten taels as a unit (i.e., one large bar). Official sales and purchases shall be conducted, and no trading outside the Association shall be allowed to prevent malpractices.

(4) Gold firms shall aim to stabilize market prices when buying and selling gold and shall not engage in speculative behavior.

(5) Each gold firm shall send members to the Association to trade daily, with a temporary limit of two persons per firm. The Association shall issue badges as proof, and no non-industry personnel shall be allowed to enter the Association to trade.

(6) The daily trading hours shall be temporarily limited to 9:30 AM to 12:00 PM in the morning and 1:30 PM to 3:00 PM in the afternoon. The market shall be closed on Sundays and holidays. All transactions shall be cleared by each party on the same day, and each gold firm shall bear full responsibility.

(7) If the price of morning trading rises or falls by more than 10% compared to the closing price of the previous afternoon, trading shall be suspended immediately. The same shall apply if the afternoon trading price rises or falls by more than 10% compared to the closing price of the morning.

(8) No interest shall be added to the price of any afternoon transaction.

(9) The fineness of gold bullion melted by gold firms shall be based on the standard of 99-factory bars. For gold bullion that does not meet the standard, the price shall be adjusted upward for higher fineness and downward for lower fineness, and the seller shall bear the cost.

(10) The Association shall not charge commissions or other fees to gold firms. All expenses related to the market shall be borne equally by all participating gold firms.

(11) If gold firms need to install intercom telephones with the Association, each firm shall be temporarily limited to one (must be directly connected to the gold firm's business premises).

(12) Gold firms participating in trading may organize a working committee to manage all matters within the market.

(13) These measures shall be jointly discussed by all members and then reported to the competent authority by the Association for approval before implementation. The same shall apply to any revisions.

Money Market Turns Steady After Easing 111

[Report from Our Newspaper] Yesterday, the money market still showed a trend of easing in the morning. Daily interest rates opened at 60 yuan, and there was no significant change in the process. There was ample supply from both inside and outside the industry.

After 3 PM, news suddenly came that the national bank had entrusted people to release gold three times, totaling 600 large bars. All were used to settle the day's positions. The money market immediately turned steady during the exchange, and the final daily interest rate rose to about 70-80 yuan.

Yesterday, national banks took in more than 1.98 billion yuan, foreign firms paid out more than 200 million yuan, major exchanges took in more than 1.25 billion yuan, and minor exchanges paid out more than 3.02 billion yuan.

Top-Quality Rice Surges Past 60,000 Yuan; Flour Prices Remain Firm; Edible Oil Prices Soar 112

The rice market continues to rise. Due to the easing of the money market, prices in the producing areas are rising, and sentiment is particularly strong. In the North Shanghai market, white rice and Pingdao rice have both risen by 3,000 yuan, with prices at 58,000 yuan. Top-quality rice is priced at over 60,000 yuan, opening at 61,000 yuan. In the South Shanghai market, the market opened with a rise of 3,000 yuan. In the Central Shanghai market, due to poor appetite among rice shops, there was a slight decline. Edible Oil: Prices are rising without end. Due to the easing of the money market, cargo owners are very reluctant to sell. Gold prices are rising, and retail investors are very eager to buy. Soybean oil opened at 230,000 yuan, immediately rising to 240,000 yuan, reaching a high of 247,000 yuan, and closing at 244,000 yuan, an increase of 27,000 yuan. Rapeseed oil rose by 22,000 yuan, each rising by more than 10%. Jitou rapeseed oil was priced at 335,000 yuan, also rising by more than 10%. Soybean cake rose by 2,000 yuan.

Flour: The market is greatly affected by the easing of the money market. Northern merchants are vigorously taking in goods. Prices of various goods outside the circle are soaring, and sentiment is firm. Cargo owners are doing their best to raise prices. Miscellaneous Grains: The upward trend continues. Soybeans jumped by 3,000-5,000 yuan due to the sharp rise in oil cake. Raw peanuts are in extremely short supply, and cargo owners are holding on to them, increasing prices by more than 20%. Sesame seeds are in strong demand in the local market, with a general increase of 10% to 20%. Red beans rose by 10%. Corn alone declined by 2,000 yuan due to sluggish sales.

Afternoon Market Suddenly Reverses; Chinese Stocks Initially Firm but Later Weakened 113

[Report from Our Newspaper] The Chinese stock market showed a trend of initial firmness followed by weakness yesterday. The money market remained loose, and hidden interest rates within the industry declined. Initially, due to the flatness and weakness of the gold and currency markets, outside speculative funds returned, and buying interest suddenly increased, causing the market to be firm in the first half of the day. Later, news came that the Central Bank was selling gold and silver without any movement. Market sentiment in gold and currency rose, and stock market sentiment weakened again. Speculative funds within the circle entered and then exited. Selling interest on the surface increased, and short sellers frequently applied pressure, causing sentiment to soften. The afternoon market still closed at a low price.

Guangdong merchants took in goods again, rising to 7.58 yuan. Large investors sold off in unison, falling slightly to 7.33 yuan. Afterwards, it hovered around 7.45 and 7.48 yuan. Near noon, due to the sharp rise in cotton yarn, yarn merchants sold again, and the market surface was filled with selling pressure, causing the market to plunge straight down to a low of 7.15 yuan, eventually closing at 7.28 yuan in the afternoon.

Small and medium-sized stocks showed a strong opening in the morning. After the opening, retail investors' appetite was still smooth, and the trend was not bad.
